<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText9911536685911269892" style="display:none"><b>Heaven Help Her.</b><br /><br />Bethany Church is an angel sent to Earth to keep dark forces at bay. Falling in love was never part of her mission, but the bond between Beth and her mortal boyfriend, Xavier Woods, is undeniably strong. But even Xavier’s love, and the care of her archangel siblings, Gabriel and Ivy, can’t keep Beth from being tricked into a motorcycle ride that ends up in Hell. There, the demon Jake Thorn bargains for Beth’s release back to Earth. But what he asks of her will destroy her, and quite possibly, her loved ones, as well.<br /><br />The story that Alexandra Adornetto built in her <i>New York Times</i> - bestselling debut, <i>Halo</i>, comes alive in action-packed and unexpected ways, as angels battle demons, and the power of love is put to the test.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I thought that Hades was better than Halo, but still not great. If you're looking for good literature, you'll be disappointed, but I read it after fin<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I thought that Hades was better than Halo, but still not great. If you're looking for good literature, you'll be disappointed, but I read it after finals week when my brain was burnt out and I didn't feel like thinking about anything and it was alright under those circumstances. There are some really cringe-worthy sentences though, just like in Halo. And yes there's a cliff-hanger.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160396380" />
    <a title="Cait" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5254851-cait"><img alt="Cait" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320186575p2/5254851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160396380?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cait" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cait" href="/user/show/5254851-cait">Cait</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160396380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17432079945094967735">I'm going to start of this review with.....<br/><br/><i> Story time! </i><br/><br/>Warning: do not try this at home. You may or may not get injured and some <i> very </i> severe scolding will follow. <b> I also begrudgingly give this book 1.5 stars as a rating. </b><br/><br/>One day, when I was about 8 or so, my family and I made our yearly trip up to Mackinac Island, Michigan. This island is different in the way that no cars or any kind of automobiles whatsoever are allowed, so everyone rides on their bikes around the 1 1/2 mile island in order</span>
  <span id="freeText17432079945094967735" style="display:none">I'm going to start of this review with.....<br><br><i> Story time! </i><br><br>Warning: do not try this at home. You may or may not get injured and some <i> very </i> severe scolding will follow. <b> I also begrudgingly give this book 1.5 stars as a rating. </b><br><br>One day, when I was about 8 or so, my family and I made our yearly trip up to Mackinac Island, Michigan. This island is different in the way that no cars or any kind of automobiles whatsoever are allowed, so everyone rides on their bikes around the 1 1/2 mile island in order to enjoy the sights. My family and I always go a couple times around the island over the course of the day, and let's just say I've never been one of the most..... observant of bike riders that you've ever seen in your life, and the town in Mackinac is always very crowded. Pretty much a disaster waiting to happen. <br><br>Everyone knows that once you get anywhere between the ages of 7-9 a weird combination comes into play. You still keep that naïvety of your youth, but you start to think of yourself as a "big boy" or "big girl" and feel like <i> you </i> should be the one in charge and you know everything about anything. Essentially, this is where you get criminally annoying and your parents want to spank your ass like there's no tomorrow. I, at that ripe and annoying age, decided I needed to lead the family through town because if anyone else did it, we'd end up lost and fall into the lake. Now, I thought I was an amazing and highly responsible leader and repeatedly checked back to make sure that my family was following, and it was during one of those times that a five year old boy, chasing a ball, ran right out in front of me and I pretty much plowed over the little guy. <br><br>This, for me, was Halo. Except I was the boy chasing the ball, also known as the pretty cover of Halo, and Adornetto was me on that bike, and she just rammed right into me with the horribleness of that book as soon as I opened to the front page.<br><br>But oh I wasn't done that day and neither was Adornetto. After a firm scolding from my parents, I dropped back into the middle of my little family pack and tried to watch where I was going. My parents still blame me for this second accident, but I honestly don't think that this one was my fault. There's a rest stop right around one of the corners of the cliffside on the island, and we planned to stop there for a break. We just get around the corner and; well, my brakes on my old bike were pieces of shit, so I looked down to plant my feet on the ground so I'd stop and as soon as I did, I biked my way right into a lady's ass. <br><br>Adornetto tried to change it up by " listening" (if you could even say that) to our advice, but she still ended up with a fail of a book and we still get fucked as readers, and people who ride bikes still get fucked up by me (on accident).<br><br>Since I started my Halo review with Bethany, I"m going to follow suit here and begin with <s> the royal pain in the ass </s> Bethany again. I'm going to cut to the chase here and say this: she's a pain in the ass. What? I already said that? Well, I'm going to say it again. She's. A. Pain. In. The. Fucking. Ass. Adornetto, in this book, after reading the reaction from people about how stupid we all thought she was in Halo, tries to increase Bethany's brain capacity (like that's even remotely possible) but she just ends up coming across as an even more stupid prick. Thinly veiled as Bethany's thoughts and words, Adornetto keeps on arguing and arguing with us about their relationship; like that she's actually got an IQ and that she can be strong and capable with quotes like this: <br><br><i> ""I knew there were people who rolled their eyes at Xavier and me, but if they did, we were too absorbed in each other’s company to notice." </i><br><b> Strike one </b><br><br><i> “It’s just not healthy for you guys to spend so much time together,” Hallie said. <br>“ Yeah,” Savannah chimed in. “It’s like you’re joined at the hip or something. I never see you apart. Wherever Xavier is, you’re right behind him. Wherever you are, he’s there … all the frigging time.” <br>"And that's a problem?" </i><br><b> Strike two </b> <br><br><i> “'Are you okay, Huggie Bear?' I asked, protectively reaching up to fix his hair. I didn’t like it when his friends played rough. </i><br><b> BHAHAHAHA strike......strike whoo.....strike *muffled snort* three </b><br><br><i> "I could never do the "'sup nod”—it made me feel as if I were in one of those music videos Molly watched on MTV where men in hoods rapped about “homies” and something called “bling.” </i><br><b> Strike three fucking million and seven </b><br><br>First off, if you receive criticism over your book, don't fucking argue with us through your chracter about how you're right and everyone else is wrong. Actually <i> do </i> something about it. And where the hell is Adornetto living? 1993? Nobody has said "bling" or "homies" for <i> years </i> now, and trust me if they still do, it's not on MTV. And don't even get me <i> started </i> on Huggie Bear. That has not and never will be a cute nickname. If anything, it reminds me more of a different kind of bear.....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379759200i/186022.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><s> Huggie Bear </s> pedobear.....<br><br>Since we're on the topic of <s> the pedo </s> Xavier, again this book is centered around that <i> looove </i> can seemingly do everything, and Bethany's obsessiveness over said love. No, Bethany, just no. Love <i> can </i> do many things, but there still are limits. Like your spirit can't manifest and become real just by looking at your hubby. You've got to have something else drive your damn story besides love, and <s> I'm not really </s> sorry to say that Hades doesn't. At all. You know you have problems when you believe that the best thing that's happened since Jake's death, even better than tripling your local church's numbers (which should be like a fat man getting free doughnuts to an angel), is that you and Xavier have grown even <i> closer </i> and you guys are now able to synchronize your steps. I'll let the beloved Dwight Schrute wrap this up for me:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348252i/702522.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ahhhh dearest Dwight I love you. Even with my enormous amount of adoration of you I will still continue to eat and drink in your honor.<br><br>And Bethany, even with all of her posturing, is <i> still </i> a giant idiot! You don't even have to go 30 pages into the book to figure that out when she uses <i> a fucking Ouija board. </i> Oh nononononononono Adornetto. I don't care if this is a fictional story or not; there are still certain rules that still always will apply, and one of those being: an angel who is a celestial being would never, ever use a Ouija board even if <i> oh-so-powerful </i> force that is peer pressure was applied. I cannot even stand the thought of that and to have it written in a story that actually got published is......astonishing. Is <i> this </i> the kind of shit that we're letting get published these days while other undiscovered authors with amazing works are getting denied?! It's just despicable and quite sad, really.<br><br>She also has little to no sense of self-preservation whatsoever, or any kind of wits:<br><br><i> "Something was wrong. I could feel it. Every celestial instinct warned me that we needed to get out of here. Fast. I found a weeping willow in the front yard and leaned against its sturdy trunk." </i><br><br>So, let's recap this little quote. If every celestial bone in your body is telling you to get the fuck out of there, what would you do? Run? Yeah, I would, too, but Bethany here decides to go <i> lean against a tree? </i> How, in any, way, shape, or form, is this running? It's not like if you go to a race you hear this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348252i/702523.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ready, set, now everyone go find a tree and stand by it, <i> quick!! </i><br><br>Then there was the whole scene with Jake being able to kidnap Bethany. I mean, how gullible can one person truly be? A boy with whom you have never spoken to before suddenly rides up on a motorcycle and claims that your boyfriend just got drunk and did something totally crazy (both of which you know he'd never do) and isn't breathing,is happy about seeing you in pain, and says you've got to go with him now; which you accept. <i> Then </i> he drives away from the lake and you see Xavier on the side of the road, and he looks perfectly fine, but a horrible look crosses over his face, and you <i> still </i> don't turn around to look at the mysterious guy behind you. Xavier yells at you to get off, you realize you can't and you <i> still </i> don't turn around. You only decide to do the smart thing and turn around to see who it is when the guy speaks and lookie there; it's Jake! Ugh. <br><br>And you know what? Nothing bad really ever happens to Bethany throughout the whole book. Sure, she's kidnapped, but she gets to live in a 5-star hotel with servants and she still technically "sees" her family almost every day. Yes, she's sentenced to death, but the flames part and never actually touch her. She's put in a cell afterwards, but she only has to stay for two measly days and is then again back in the opulence of the hotel. Oh, but <i> then </i> you think, Jake's actually going to have sex with her, right? But, no, she gets saved in the nick of time and gets to go back home and graduate. And just to add insult to injury (see if this sounds even the most smidgen familiar *cough cough* Twlight *cough cough*) Xavier asks her to marry her with an old-fashioned cut diamond ring given to him by his grandmother. <br><br>There's so many good things happening here I think I might puke. I just wanted even the tiniest bit of character development from her due to a hardship or some kind of calamity happening, but I got absolutely nothing. Everything just <i> has </i> to work out perfectly for little miss perfect-pants, and I just couldn't stand it at all. She shouldn't always get to go home and have a happily ever after in every damn book! Dwight, sum it up for me, will ya?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348252i/702524.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>For now.....<br><br>Just like a book that I had read previously, and also reviewed with a great amount of fury, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15047.The_Passion" title="The Passion by Jeanette Winterson" rel="nofollow noopener">Passion</a>, Adornetto severely fucked up Lucifer. Where Kate's was just a fail in making him look scary, Adornetto's is a total fail through and through. Here's how she described him:<br><br><i> " He wore a white linen suit with a red silk tie and his feet were encased in white cowboy boots. He held an ivory-topped cane that he tapped softly on the cement floor... His skin was tanned and leathery and his eyes were a pellucid blue but devoid of any expression. He was immaculately groomed and wore his silver hair tied back loosely with a gilded clasp." </i><br><br>Sooooo.....he looks like a younger version of Colonel Sanders from KFC?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348252i/702525.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Fear me; for I make people <i> fat! </i><br><br>And get this: they call him..... <i> Big Daddy. </i> *snorts* and if that's not horrible enough, he pretty much does nothing or; at least, nothing I feel like Lucifer would <i> ever </i> do. You know you're in a sorry state when you get one-upped by <i> Bethany </i> and you can't even kill her royal annoyingness who practically does it herself almost every day. He probably should have just left her alone with herself and she would have done the job by the end of the day.<br> <br>Adornetto's writing is; once again, horrible. The info-dumps in the first ten pages <i> alone </i> are so gut-wrenchingly awful that if you didn't quit then and there, hell, you deserve a silver star. And they continue through the whole book and slows down the flow so much it's like trying to walk through molasses. She also frequently forgets her writing and either contradicts herself or repeats something that she said only a mere sentence ago:<br><br><i> "Its tall windows were opaque from a fine layer of accumulated dust and grime. The room itself was empty except for an iron bedstead pushed up against a grimy window." </i><br><br>*shakes head* oh Adornetto, Adornetto, Adornetto. You already <i> told </i> us that the windows were grimy, so why tell us yet again with this specific window; why even mention it at all? If she hadn't mentioned it at all, the sentence would have been fine, but she always has to ruin it somehow, now doesn't she? She does it again about ten pages later when Jake's got her on the motorcycle. She goes on for about two paragraphs about how she can't die and that she can survive Armageddon, any natural disaster, etc. but contradicts <i> herself </i> by saying that she won't try to tip over the motorcycle because she'll get "smeared all over the road"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348252i/702526._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bethany! Why didn't you do it?! You'll fucking <i> live! </i> You literally cannot die as long as you and your idiot brain is <s> contaminating </s> walking the earth! Stop being a pussy and just do it! I know that this is partly Adornetto's and her editor's fault for not catching the contradiction, but it shouldn't have even been a problem in the first place. Bethany should have done whatever it took to get off of that motorcycle, but instead she just sat there and passed out. <br><br>Also, for someone who says she doesn't like writing about dark topics; she certainly did it quite a bit in this book. There were exorcisms, pits of hell with flaying, beating, and burning people alive, weird erotic pain, and all-around dark topics. She just really loves to contradict herself, doesn't she?<br><br>And don't even get me <i> started </i> on this whole Gabriel and Molly mess. I'm sorry, Adornetto, but making Gabriel fall in love with someone, that's crossing a major line with me. Whatever Bethany is a lower rank greeter angel so I guess falling in love is......okay (yeah, right). But to have one of <i> the </i> highest arch-angels out there fall in love with a hormonal, idiotic, 18 year old girl didn't work for me before this book and definitely isn't going to work for me now. If it continues....<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>The plot is some of the most boring and repetitive stuff I've ever seen. This is how it went (warning this is a little long because the book is so damn long):<br><br>Bethany: I love you<br><br>Xavier: I love you<br><br>Bethany: I love you<br><br>Xavier: I love you<br><br>Xavier: let's go to a party<br><br>Bethany: okay, I'll do whatever you do. <br><br>Bethany: wow, these kids look like a bunch of lions in play (no kidding that's what she says)<br><br>Molly: let's do a seance! <br><br>Bethany: I don't know...<br><br>Everyone else: *peer pressure*<br><br>Bethany: like alright!<br><br>Mysterious boy: get on the motorcycle<br><br>Bethany: like okay!<br><br>Jake: muhahahahah it's me I'm eeeeeevilll!<br><br>Bethany: ahh I had no idea it was you even with all the glaring signs!<br><br>Jake: love me<br><br>Bethany: no, I hate you!<br><br>Jake: *says mean things*<br><br>Bethany: *gets sad*<br><br>*wash, rinse and repeat about ten times*<br><br>Bethany: *creates a butterfly*<br><br>Lucifer (sorry I refuse to call him Big Daddy): you must die!<br><br>Bethany: noooo! *lives*<br><br>Bethany: *magically appears to Xavier* I love you! <br><br>Xavier: no I love you!<br><br>Bethany: no I lov-<br><br>Jake: no you love me. Die, Xavier!<br><br>Bethany: Nooo!<br><br>Jake: have sex with me!<br><br>Bethany: nooo! <br><br>Jake: *peer pressure*<br><br>Bethany: okay! <br><br>Jake: *starts to kiss her in the little grotto*<br><br>Gabriel: never fear for I have come to save you!<br><br>Xavier: me, too!<br><br>Gabriel: whatever. *stabs Jake*<br><br>Jake: help me, Bethany! <br><br>Bethany: like okay! <br><br>Gabriel: *stops her*<br><br>Xavier: marry me!<br><br>Bethany: okay!<br> <br>Me: *slaps forehead*<br><br>So, why did I rate this book 1.5 stars? Well, because the one exorcism scene was actually well written, so if you want one nice scene, read a ton of shit and you'll get one.<br><br>I'm done with this book now with this review being done, and if I ever pick this book up again, so help me God somebody slap me. I wash my hands of this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17432079945094967735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">*starts to cry* I-I wouldn't recommend this book to the person that SLAUGHTERED MY FAMILY</span></div>

      ...this was my own fault...

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201203047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16701561829628141785"><b>Before reading Hades</b><br/><br/>How can you <i>trick</i> someone into getting on a motorcycle? Either they get on, or they don't get on. Motorcycles aren't like cars. And what does angel Bethany want with a motorcycle anyway? SHE CAN FLY. Or, I'm assuming she can. Who knows, maybe Halo angels are just so lame they can't even use their wings to fly. *shudders from pure lameness*<br/><br/>Perhaps the conversation went something like this:<br/><br/>Jake: Hey Bethany. Why don't you get <s>in my van</s> on my motorcycle? I'll give you a lift...<br/>B</span>
  <span id="freeText16701561829628141785" style="display:none"><b>Before reading Hades</b><br><br>How can you <i>trick</i> someone into getting on a motorcycle? Either they get on, or they don't get on. Motorcycles aren't like cars. And what does angel Bethany want with a motorcycle anyway? SHE CAN FLY. Or, I'm assuming she can. Who knows, maybe Halo angels are just so lame they can't even use their wings to fly. *shudders from pure lameness*<br><br>Perhaps the conversation went something like this:<br><br>Jake: Hey Bethany. Why don't you get <s>in my van</s> on my motorcycle? I'll give you a lift...<br>Bethany: No wayz.<br>Jake: I have...teh ice cream! And kitties!<br>Bethany: OOOOHHHH KITTIES! *hops on*<br>Jake: MUAHAHA SILLY GIRL THERE ARE NO KITTIES<br>Bethany: NOOOOO I HAZ BEEN TRICKED!<br>Jake: MUAHAHHAHAHAHAHAAAAA<br><br>Now that would make a lot of sense.<br><br>10/11<br><br>I AM GOING TO DO IT.<br><br>I'm going to rip this to shreds with my razor teeth! It sounds so bad I cannot resist.<br><br><b>After reading Hades</b><br><br><br>Warning: There will be heaps of Allie-bashing, lots of cap rage, Hades-bashing, swearing, and SWEARING, and DID I MENTION SWEARING?!<br><br>Glossary: Because I won't explain who all of the characters are inbetween my rage outs.<br><br>Bethie: The main character.<br><br>Xavier: Her boring ass boyfriend.<br><br>Jake Thorn: The Prince of Hell<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>......fuck....<br><br><br>.....FUUUUUCCCCCKKKKKKK.....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708738.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>You notice how light and joking I was in my pre-review? Notice how I was poking fun at Bethie, notice how I was...<i>happy</i>....?<br><br>I WILL NEVER BE THE SAME WAY AGAIN.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708739.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="Noah Pukcerman screaming in rage at Hades's terribleness." class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I had originally planned on writing a nice, coherent, numerical list of this book's fails but THAT IS IMPOSSIBLE. I WOULD BE HERE ALL FREAKING DAY.<br><br>So, I will rant on random things.<br><br>Firstly, <br><br><br>ADORNETTO NEEDS TO SHUT. THE FUCK. UP.<br><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708740.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not a single freaking page goes by without this neurotic, raging bitch (insult courtesy of Hana Joy :D) preaching to us about something or the other. IT'S DISGUSTING. Here are a few examples of Allie dearest reaching her nasty author hand through the pages:<br><br>1. Her version of Hell<br><br>The way she describes the inhabitants of hell. Miniskirts, piercings, chains, black nail polish -- generally goth. We all know how Christian and conservative Allie dearest is, so it's obvious why she would choose to condemn these things -- they just don't fit in with her idea of what's "moral" and "perfect".<br><br>2. Her lectures on sex<br><br>While reading that entire part I was essentially doing this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/502596.gif" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I WANTED TO STAB MY EYES OUT WITH A FUCKING PEN.<br><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151480239" rel="nofollow noopener">In Kira's review, which is much, much better than this one and you should in fact read it NOW</a> she says "<i>Bethany is viciously devoid of conscience. You'd think she'd be "all soul", as Xavier once said (BARF) but in fact she's completely devoid of any kind of compassion. She lets Jake bleed to death and die before her, she leaves her friends to rot in Hell (literally), and she says, and I quote, "The purpose of sex is to create life." <br><br>Oh, really? You want me to go there? Seriously? <br><br>FUCK THIS MOTHERFUCKING SHIT YOU BIG PIECE OF FESTERING MONKEY VOMIT. <br><br>This is a disgraceful thing to write. Who the fuck green-lighted this shit? Someone needs to be fired for this. I'm not even kidding. <br><br>About two weeks ago, a teenager who featured on Youtube as a strong advocate of the It Gets Better campaign killed himself. He had been so viciously bullied and isolated because of his sexuality that he chose to end his own life. He was so utterly crushed by misery, shame and loneliness that he committed suicide. He was little more than a child. <br><br>This comment advertising sex as a way to procreate and nothing more is a violation of so many people's beliefs and lifestyles, and is a complete disgrace in every sense of the word. Not only does it completely exclude homosexuality and indirectly condemn it, but it also reverts back to this fabricated idea of "virginity". Basically, it is a vicious way to shame and attack gay and lesbian peoples for the way that they choose to express perfectly natural attraction to the people they romantically love and/or date. Homosexuality is in no way wrong, it is in no way unnatural, and condemning it borders on a violation of human rights. Quebec had it down when they said, "The state has no place in the bedrooms of the nation." <br><br>Amen, sista's. </i>"<br><br>That was a rather long quote, I know, but it all needed to be there because I don't know any other way to express my annoyance. Sure, I had read Kira's review before throwing myself into the pit of shit and vomit that is alternatively known as Hades, but reading the quote in context provided with everything else makes me want to <i>hurt myself</i>.<br><br>IT'S JUST SO TERRIBLE.<br><br>That, that doesn't even <i>count</i> the heaps of other sex lecturing. JAKE EVEN REFERS TO BETHIES "VIRGINITY" AS HER "VIRTUE". It's fucking disgusting how obsessed Allie is with this. <br><br>SHE PUTS A SHAME TO ALL TEENAGERS EVERYWHERE. (She is a teenager still, right? I don't know and I don't give a fuck. SHE PUTS A SHAME TO EVERYONE CONSIDERED NOT AN ADULT YET EVERYWHERE.)<br><br>In short, if I ever met Allie in real life and caught her trying to give anyone a fucking lecture on fucking ANYTHING, I'd do this:<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708741.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And this:<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708742.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And <i>this</i>:<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708743.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gross little bitch...<br><br>What else did I want to rant about?<br><br><br>Oh ya. BETHIE DEAREST.<br><br>Bethany is so <i>stupid</i>. So yeah, I have an ebook copy of this utter vomit and shit, right? That's bad, very bad, because as long as we're in Bethie's head every few sentences I have the urge to throw the book against the wall with a satisfying thud. BUT IT'S AN EBOOK COPY. So I would end up doing this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708744.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Which would suck, seeing as how I only gots one computer, yeah. <br><br>Her stupidity was <u>SO OFFENSIVE</u> that it made me literally burst out into tears.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708745.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Well...maybe not literally -- BUT I WAS FUCKING CLOSE.<br><br>And the worst part, because Bethie is Adornetto's self insert (anyone try to argue with me over this in the comments and I will cuss you the fuck out, just so you know) WE GET DOUBLE THE PREACHING. So while Adornetto is using her author powers to preach through the story, BETHIE IS FUCKING PREACHING IN THE STORY.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357454ra/708746.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>IT MADE ME WANT TO THROW THINGS.<br><br>Not to mention that Bethie is A FUCKING MARY SUE.<br><br>Even when she goes to Hell, EVEN IN HELL THEY LIKE HER. EVERYBODY LIKES HER. THE PRINCE OF THE FUCKING HELL WANTS HER. IS THERE ONE PERSON THAT DOESN'T LIKE BETHANY WHO ISN'T DEMONIZED?!?!?!?! AND WE WILL FUCKING TALK ABOUT ASIA LATER.<br><br>FUCK THAT. WE'LL TALK ABOUT HER RIGHT NOW BEFORE I FUCKING FORGET OR SOMETHING WITH MY GOLDFISH BRAIN, BECAUSE READING HADES HAS FUCKING BRAIN DAMAGED ME WITH IT'S TERRIBLE, HORRIBLE AWFULNESS AND I CAN BARELY REMEMBER MY FUCKING NAME ANYMORE BECAUSE IT IS <u>JUST THAT BAD</u>.<br><br>FUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUUCCCCCCCCCKKKKKKKK THIISSSSSSS BOOOOOOOKKKKKKKKKKKEEEEEEHHHHHHAAAAAAAAOOOOUUUUSSSSSHHOIFWIAIOFNWA<br><br><br>So, to talk about Asia.<br><br>Asia is Jake's bitch, basically. Also, from what I remember she is one of the only minorities in the book, if not <i>the</i> only minority, someone can correct me on this if they want. <br><br>How is she portrayed?<br><br>Well, even though she's supposed to be a snide, evil bitch (and slut?) I actually quite liked her. She acknowledged Bethany as the stupid, disgusting, waste of space she was, see this quote: <i>I gave the woman a closer look and remembered her instantly as the tattooed barmaid from Pride. It would have been hard to forget the annihilating look she’d given me then. She gave me a fleeting glance this time as if my presence were too immaterial to take up any more of her time.</i> I agree with her. Bethany doesn't deserve anyone's time. She's a gross, nasty, hideous waste of space and she should be burned on the stake, cut in half, erased from this universe forever and ever. AMEN. <br><br>Also, Asia gets jealous that Jake likes Bethany more than her. IT'S A VALID COMPLAINT. So you're the head bitch of hell with your psuedo boyfriend, and then some sniveling preachy brat shows up and snatches your honey's attention. Oh, yeah, tell me <i>you</i> wouldn't be bitter. There's also the added fact THAT THEY ARE ALL FUCKING DEMONS SO DUHHHH. <br><br>But we're supposed to see Asia as a jealous, evil, bitch. That's great. That's just fucking fantastic. Way to go Allie dear. But you wanna know something? I'd rather be represented by an Asia FIVE THOUSAND FUCKING TIMES OVER than be represented by a Bethie, which is <i>the worse fucking insult ever, in the history of time and space, the worst thing in the whole world ever to exist AMEN.</i><br><br>Anything else?<br><br>Well, there's Xavier. He annoys the shit out of me. And Jake is an asshole, as well as a rapist, but once again he's a demon so you know. That's rather accurate for Jake.<br><br>Oh! How could I forget?<br><br>Xavier and Bethie's relationship.<br><br>THAT IS THE MOST...I DON'T EVEN HAVE WORDS FOR IT. It is co-dependent, unhealthy, obsessive, weird, and just NO. NO JUST NO.<br><br>How can you write something like this and portray it as being positive? HOW? HOW CAN YOU POSSIBLY PORTRAY THIS AS NORMAL, EVEN A GOOD THING? Another reason why I want to punch Allie in the face, or at least strap her into a chair and viciously re-educate her. <br><br>PLEASE GOD. IF YOU DO EXIST, WHICH I DON'T REALLY THINK YOU DO BUT <i>IF YOU DO</i>, PLEASE, DO NOT ALLOW ALEXANDRA ADORNETTO TO PROCREATE UNTIL SHE GAINS AT LEAST AN OUNCE OF FUCKING COMMON SENSE. PLEASE. PLEASE. PLEASE.<br><br>Amen.<br><br>Here are some examples of how co-dependent and fucked up Xavier and Allie I MEAN BETHIE'S relationship is:<br><br><i>I kept one of Xavier’s Tshirts, dowsed in his cologne, under my pillow so that every night I could imagine he was with me. It was funny how the goofiest behavior could feel perfectly natural when you were in love.</i><br><br><i>“Okay, don’t take the quiz,” Hallie cut in. “Just answer a few questions, okay?” “Shoot,” I said. “What’s your favorite football team?” “Dallas Cowboys,” I said without hesitation. “And why’s that?” Hallie asked. “Because it’s Xavier’s favorite team.”</i><br><br><i>“He’s coming over to make barbecue ribs.” “Since when do you like ribs?” The girls raised their eyebrows. “Xavier likes them.”</i><br><br><i>I was willing to pardon any crime, but one against Xavier, and so help me, God, Jake would get his comeuppance.</i><br><br><i>Every fiber in my body yearned to return to Xavier. My one true love. The light of my life. (..) My pain was so all consuming that I hardly cared where Jake was taking me to or what horrors awaited. </i><br><br>Had enough? I think so. I know if I type anymore about this shit I will vomit all over my computer, shorting it out. If I do vomit over my computer from Hades induced sickness I WILL sue Adornetto for enough money to get a new one, I swear it.<br><br>Is there something else?<br><br>Oh yeah!<br><br>I DON'T CARE.<br><br>The book was so boring, so annoying, so rage inducing, it was so terrible. I WANTED TO DIE.<br><br>Top Causes of Death:<br>Heart disease<br>Cancer<br>Stroke<br>Chronic lower respiratory diseases<br>Accidents<br>Alzheimer's disease<br>Diabetes<br>Influenza and Pneumonia<br>Nephritis, nephrotic syndrome, and nephrosis<br>Septicemia<br>Hades by Alexandra Adornetto<br><br><br><br>It's the truth, people.<br><br><br>Oh, and there's one more thing I wanted to mention...<br><br>One more thing...<br><br>What was it...<br><br>That...thing about....<br><br>Wait...<br><br>It's on the tip of my tongue....<br><br>OH!<br><br>I remember now!<br><br>It was...<br><br>THAT GODDAMN FUCKING SHIT VOMIT CREATURE HELL ANGER RAGE RAGE RAGE CAPSLOCK DOLPHIN FUCKING FUCK FUCK FUCKING TITLE!<br><br>Many fanidiots have gotten upset about people constantly pointing out that Hades =/= Hell. They say Adornetto can call her books anything she wants. They say Adornetto can do anything she wants. They say that people who point out Hades =/= Hell, lovers of Greek Mythology who hate to see this mixed up, people with general common sense, they say that they need to shut up and worship Allie like they do.<br><br>To that I say this:<br><br>FUCCCCCCCCKKKKKKKKKK YYYYYYYYYOOOOOOOUUUUUUUUUUU PPPPPPEEEEEEEOOOOOOOPPPPPPLLEEEEEEEEEAAAAHHHHUAISUFNIOSNAOSIPG<br><br><br>Guess what? Guess what? I added this section just because of you, you blithering bleeding dolts! So here I will say it:<br><br>HADES IS NOT HELL. HADES IS GREEK MYTHOLOGY FOR THE AFTERLIFE, NOT HELL, NOT EVIL, NOT PAINFUL, JUST THE WHOLE AFTERLIFE. HELL IS CHRISTIAN MYTHOLOGY FOR AN ACTUAL PLACE OF ETERNAL SUFFERING, BAD, PAINFUL, ALL THAT CRAP. YOU CAN NOT MIX THEM UP OR SUBSTITUTE ONE FOR THE OTHER BECAUSE THEY ARE NOT THE SAME THING, THEY DO NOT MEAN THE SAME THING, AND THEY WILL <u>NEVER, EVER, EVER, EVER MEAN THE SAME THING</u>!!<br><br>AND FUCK ANYONE ELSE THAT THINKS OTHERWISE. DO A WIKIPEDIA SEARCH YOU JACKASSES.<br><br>Wow. That got really aggressive at the end there, actually. (Well this whole review has actually been really aggressive. GOT A PROBLEM WITH IT?)<br><br>Sure, Allie has the right to write whatever she wants, AND I HAVE THE RIGHT TO FUCKING RIDICULE AND BELITTLE HER FOR IT. BAHAHAHAHAHA. <br><br>That is the end of my review.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/215412.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357455ra/708747.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND NOW FOR A RANDOM TOKKA GIF.<br><br><i>Because I can and I feel like it.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380357455ra/708748.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>HAH.<br><br><b>WARNING: TROLL MY REVIEW AND I AM FULLY PREPARED TO AND WILL TROLL YOU THE FUCK BACK. SO BE FOREWARNED, ASSHOLES OF THE INTERNET. <i>YOU HAZ BEEN WARNED.</i></b><br><br><br>Note: Everyone that reads this review should rate Hades 1 star, don't care if you have read the book or not, the rating on this pile of shit and vomit is too fucking high and we as human beings need to do something about this.<br><br>If you want to you can even read the book to write a bad review of it, which I encourage, this needs as many bad reviews as it can get, seriously. But do not buy the book, Jesus Fucking Christ do not buy the book please. Pirate this thing. Do not waste your money. <u>Do not waste your hard earned dollars on this creature, please, for the life of me, DO NOT</u>.<br><br>(Yes I am bitter and angry about Hades and I will continue to be bitter and angry about Hades FOR THE REST OF MY LIFE. AMEN.)</span>

good time<br/>Enjoy reading<br/><br/>Now that almost all of the</span>
  <span id="freeText135558784117414409" style="display:none">So I wonder if I've ever told you people how much I love making lists. Yep. I spend hours on my things to do and other random lists. <br><br>Here's one I'm sharing with you. <br><br><b>
  <u>Things I'd probably do while trying to read HADES</u>
</b><br><br>Leaf through the pages<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356827i/708258.png" width="20" height="20" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Endure <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356827i/708258.png" width="20" height="20" alt="description" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356827i/708258.png" width="20" height="20" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Go to sleep <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356827i/708258.png" width="20" height="20" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Watch tv <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356827i/708258.png" width="20" height="20" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Read another book <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356827i/708258.png" width="20" height="20" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Have a good time<br>Enjoy reading<br><br>Now that almost all of these have been <b>checked off</b> the list except the last two that somehow evade me EVERY TIME I TRY! I decided I couldn't wait forever to write a review on here. <br><br><u>BEHOLD! The RESULTS OF MY MANY ATTEMPTS TO <s>READ</s> HADES</u> [IN CHRONOLOGICAL ORDER]<br><br>Attempt # 1:<br><br><i>“Are you coming over for dinner tonight?” I asked Xavier, linking my arm through his. “Gabriel wants to try making burritos.”</i><br><br>*major eye roll* Get your own gourmet show already Gabriel! Or get a life, whatever comes first. Growing a pair might help too.<br><br>Attempt # 2:<br><br><i>“I’m just thinking,” he said. “How come in all the paintings, angels are depicted guarding thrones in Heaven or taking out demons? I wonder why they’re never shown in the kitchen making burritos.”<br>“Because we have a reputation to uphold,” I said, nudging him. “So are you coming?”</i><br><br>Hmmm, I wonder what reputation she's talking about? Oh I know! the dumb ass, good for nothing angel trio reputation! Lets see how the story goes. Once upon a time, 3 great angels descended from the heavens, <s>each bringing a gift to mankind</s> No, no, no. That is all wrong. <br><br>There were these three angels, the elder one liked cooking, the middle one liked partying, the little one made everyone's life miserable. <br><br>Oh wait, I think I got my 80 year old neighbors confused with these characters. <br><br>Attempt # 3<br><br><i>"He was just as breathtakingly beautiful as ever. His tie hung loose and his blazer was slung casually over one shoulder."</i><br><br>*blinks* <br>*tries to recall what Xavier looked like*<br>*an image of a faceless teenager with mouse colored hair pops in mind* <br>*shakes head sadly* <br><br>This girl needs to get some, if she thinks a tie hanging loose and blazer slung casually on one shoulder makes for breathtakingly beautiful. <br><br>Attempt # 4 <br><br><i>“Gabriel wants to try making burritos.”</i><br><br>Hmmm ¬¬<br><br>I'm hungry. I should go get some burritos too. *cheerfully walk to the kitchen*<br><br>Attempt # 5<br><br><i>Since the violent encounter with Jake last year, Xavier had hit the gym even harder and thrown himself into sports more vigorously.</i><br><br>*stupefied beyond belief*<br>a little pause<br><br>*laughs hysterically* <br><br>I'm sure the occupants of Hell are waiting in agony for Xavier's Ultimate Fitness Show. LIVE. <br><br>Attempt # 6<br><br><i>"His face was open and friendly. I was pleased to see that Gabriel was more relaxed these days."</i><br><br>*gasp* Is he?! I tell you! it's those ballet classes, and sewing he's taken up. Isn't he divine! *swoons*<br><br>Attempt # 7<br><br><i>"I kept one of Xavier’s T-shirts, dowsed in his cologne, under my pillow so that every night I could imagine he was with me."</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379789264i/520526._SX540_.png" width="430" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*PUKES* </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14375317899889779744">WHAT!? She is tricked in riding a motorcycle? How? <br/><br/>I am sorry, but it ticks me off how stupid and childish she made what's-her-face. I understand she is a angel just "born", but seriously? Can you at least make her a little bad ass? I like bad ass heriones. Not the little crying whinny girls.   <span id="freeText14375317899889779744" style="display:none">WHAT!? She is tricked in riding a motorcycle? How? <br /><br />I am sorry, but it ticks me off how stupid and childish she made what's-her-face. I understand she is a angel just "born", but seriously? Can you at least make her a little bad ass? I like bad ass heriones. Not the little crying whinny girls. I understand that there are moments where that it is called for, but through out the whole series of books? <br /><br />What the hell are you thinking Andornetto? Why don't you grow up a bit before publishing what you think teenage girls and boys are today. We are not idiots, or "sheltered" from the outside world? Be realistic? <br /><br />UGH! And I hate myself that I am going to go out of my way to read this becuase of my fatal flaw of curiosity, and how I cannot stop reading a series after the first book. Curiosity killed the cat, you know? I swear that if this books SUCKS (which, god, I know it will) I will personally call the Andornetto chick up and scream her freakin ear off. Then e-mail her until she finally realizes the mistakes she made in this series? <br /><br />And Hades? Really? I thought this was about angels? Oh, wait. No its not, its about religion. Christanity to be exact. She is sooo stupid. She has officially ruined my obession with angels. Thanks a lot, Obession ruiner!!!!!!!!!! </span>

<div id="review_192955658" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192955658" />
    <a title="Katya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4324634-katya"><img alt="Katya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285183076p2/4324634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192955658?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katya" href="/user/show/4324634-katya">Katya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=the-ya-project">the-ya-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4324634-katya?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192955658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12439603548283132143">I... I ah... I can't even... What am I supposed to say here? This is just one of these books you knew, going into it, that you were never going to like it, and yet, after you finish it, you remain with a sour taste in your mouth. <br/><br/>Of course, that begs the question as to why I bothered reading it in the first place (in fact, I expect that question soon), and I will adress it... later on. Let me tell you, pure masochism has little to do with it.<br/><br/>On the positive side, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9666812.Hades__Halo___2_' title='Hades (Halo, #2) by Alexandra Adornetto' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hades</a> is better than its predece</span>
  <span id="freeText12439603548283132143" style="display:none">I... I ah... I can't even... What am I supposed to say here? This is just one of these books you knew, going into it, that you were never going to like it, and yet, after you finish it, you remain with a sour taste in your mouth. <br><br>Of course, that begs the question as to why I bothered reading it in the first place (in fact, I expect that question soon), and I will adress it... later on. Let me tell you, pure masochism has little to do with it.<br><br>On the positive side, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9666812.Hades__Halo___2_" title="Hades (Halo, #2) by Alexandra Adornetto" rel="nofollow noopener">Hades</a> is better than its predecesor, as far as plot and pacing are concerned. There is a clearly defined antagonist, clearly defined stakes that get bigger as the book progresses, not to mention there is an inciting incident early on into the story (In other words, something happens).<br><br>But while the book is better plot-and-pacing-wise, the writing still suffers from the problems in Halo: adjectives and adverbs litter the text whenever a description or a simile didn't cut the trick, along with a case of telling-not-showing that I suspect can be classified in a genre of its own.<br><br><i> Xavier never liked Maddison much. She drank and smoked too much and always gave her opinion when it wasn't wanted. </i> (Hades)<br><br>Alright, point out the problems in these sentences. One by one, please and take turns, children, everyone will have a say.<br><br>Yes, Bethany is telling us why Xavier doesn't like Maddison, and yes, a lot of us might slightly be offended, but it's not just the character telling us what another character is. It's the author telling the readers what they should think. Xavier is perfect, so obviously his opinion is paramount, so if he dislikes Maddison for drinking and smoking and being outspoken, then the reader MUST dislike her as well. Of course, Adornetto doesn't stop there and does her very best to make Maddison seem as asinine as possible to cement that opinion.<br><br>That's a huge strike against Hades, if only because many of us have been a little like Maddison as teenagers. Outspoken, I mean, although I have had my share of alcoholic experiments at seventeen. <br><br>But it's not just that - stories stimulate us on many levels, igniting our imaginations and making us live within them. Mindless or high-brow, a story makes a reader THINK and draw their own conclusions and opinions about it, and about its characters. What I mean to say is, authors shouldn't insult our intelligence by telling us what to think. Or at least, they can make it so that the MC's initial impression of that character was flawed and that they had some more depth.<br><br>Speaking of depth, I would like to express my disappointment with the women in this book. Yes, Bethany is probably the easiest target, but what about Asia, and all the jealous bitches she epitomizes? What about Hanna, whose traits are subservant, tortured and repentant? <br><br>What about Molly? Her character, in particular, frustrates me to no end. She had so much potential! She was actually faced with a real crisis, and she could have grown past her image of a sex-crazed adolescent. Instead, she remains as short-sighted and silly as ever, a fact which is hammered into the reader's head again (Scount Mints?) and again (reapplying lip gloss while a serious conversation is happening) and again (whenever Gabriel is around). Maybe I could have bought it in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7778981.Halo__Halo___1_" title="Halo (Halo, #1) by Alexandra Adornetto" rel="nofollow noopener">Halo</a>, where she was just a girl and the stakes weren't so high, but not when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she knows that Gabriel, Beth and Ivy are angels! I mean that's your best friend's life hanging on the line, get serious girl!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>In fact, the only reason Molly seems to exist is to push a relationship between her and Gabriel, which pisses me off to no end. For the love of... the age difference alone should be enough to put people off, but there's more. Those two characters have absolutely no chemistry. At no point does Gabriel show that he has any special feelings for Molly, which makes her sound like a crazy person <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when she confronts him about it  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Seeing those two interact is like reading every other stalker/stalkee romance in the genre, only with the roles reversed, and if Gabriel does turn out to have feelings for Molly, I'll just /CENSORED/!<br><br>Even putting aside the fact that their 'love' is probably the most implausible thing in the entire book (and that's saying a lot), there is still the matter of how women are portrayed - they can either be slutty, meek, weak, or love interests, there is no middle ground, and none of them seem to play a vital part in the story. Ivy, a bloody seraphim, can't stand on her own two feet after an exorcism, while Gabe can not only hold her up, but help Molly while she's vomiting in the bushes. Wow!<br><br>Do I even have to get started on Bethany, the biggest hypocrite of them all? I'm not even angry with her, I'm just sad. In one of my status updates, I speculate about an alternate universe where Beth is human and was just adopted by the angels. Not only would that explain her weakness and lack of knowledge, but it would make her a lot more likeable character. Adornetto obviously tries to make Bethanie a relatable character, but she's a freaking angel! She should be able to hold her own against the forces of darkness, take action, be proactive. If she were human, her desire to be with Xavier would be understandable, as well as her thirst for a normal life. The whole graduation scene is about leaving childhood behind and starting life as adults, but Bethanie is an angel, she shouldn't care about that. <br><br>I've been talking about this for too long, so let's just wrap this up. Hades is definitely better than Halo, but not by much. Whatever strengths it has in the plot and pacing are lost on the eye-poking writing, plotholes and horrible, horrible characters. It honestly pains me to write this because the author is so young, but you know, I'm tired of making excuses for her. 80% of the population want to be writers and there is a good reason why only 2 make it to publication - stories don't just need to exist. They must have a reason to be told, and that's why I keep on reading - because stories have to be read. But Adornetto's characters are already perfect - they don't question the status quo, they don't even attempt it. There are no twists, no self-doubt, no real self-examination. They go nowhere, and learn nothing, and that's ultimately what the problem is. <br><br><br><br><br><br><b> And now, bonus time. </b><br><br><b> Before: </b><br><br>Dear Ms Adornetto,<br><br>I am warning you beforehand. If this kid puts Hades to <a href="http://www.smh.com.au/opinion/politics/keep-your-politics-out-of-our-classrooms-mr-nile-20110801-1i77c.html#poll" rel="nofollow noopener">shame</a>, I will not only lose any respect I have for you being published at 13, but I will also consider you a stain upon the name of Australia and all its awesome people. <br><br>Yours,<br>A Reader<br><br><b> After: </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380355421i/707637.jpg" width="374" height="411" alt="crying" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i> I weep for literature. </i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12439603548283132143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_120195478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120195478" />
    <a title="hayden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden"><img alt="hayden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598996671p2/2995566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120195478?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="hayden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="hayden" href="/user/show/2995566-hayden">hayden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Halo (Hades is definitely better); Twilight; Hush, Hush; Evermore; and Fallen</span></div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120195478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4453132148268309942">Dear World,<br/>Please do not question my sanity. I promise I have not lost it. I am reading this for the freaking lulz AND THAT'S IT.<br/>Sincerely, Me.<br/><br/><b>While I'm writing my review, you may entertain yourselves by reading my </b>46<b> status updates below. Thank you, come again.<br/><br/>Also, notice the addition of three stars. That means my review is coming </b>REAL SOON,<b> I promise!</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Review: 1.5 stars</u>
</b><br/><i>First impressions are deceiving.</i><br/>I have fourteen years’ worth of anecdotal proof that this theory is true, but the one examp</span>
  <span id="freeText4453132148268309942" style="display:none">Dear World,<br>Please do not question my sanity. I promise I have not lost it. I am reading this for the freaking lulz AND THAT'S IT.<br>Sincerely, Me.<br><br><b>While I'm writing my review, you may entertain yourselves by reading my </b>46<b> status updates below. Thank you, come again.<br><br>Also, notice the addition of three stars. That means my review is coming </b>REAL SOON,<b> I promise!</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Review: 1.5 stars</u>
</b><br><i>First impressions are deceiving.</i><br>I have fourteen years’ worth of anecdotal proof that this theory is true, but the one example I want to give you is Alexandra Adornetto’s first book, HALO (which I’m sure everyone and their mom has read or at least seen).<br><br>Back when I was an innocent little thirteen-year-old, I was wandering the bottom floor of my Barnes &amp; Noble, looking at the new releases and such, molesting the Nooks, blahblah. Bored of my futile search (I’d never been much of an adult reader, and the bottom floor was where all the mainstream adult books were kept at the time), I headed over toward the escalator that took you to the top floor, with the children’s section; the adult PNR section; the board games section; and the teen/YA section. YA had proved to be a friendly companion in my recent years of extremely frequent reading, and I was itching to get to the top and find some more to read.<br><br>When I reached the top of the escalator, I saw a six-shelf display of HALO, and I nearly jizzed my pants. <br><br>It was <i>beautiful</i>. <br><br>I almost couldn’t tolerate <i>not</i> owning it. <br><br>When I was an adult and I was rich and famous and I branched out into the publishing world, I <i>had</i> to get that cover designer on board with me to design my book. <br><br>I wouldn’t live if I didn’t.<br><br>I stood there for a good minute or so just marveling at the beautiful wonder that was the cover of HALO before I finally couldn’t stand it any longer and I had to touch it. When I picked it up, I could almost hear the angels singing “Alleluia” in my ears (no pun intended, folks). I knew I had to buy it.<br><br>And I did. I bought the hell out of it.<br><br>I wish I could tell you right now that the contents of that book were as beautiful as the cover was. I wish I could tell you I gave it a no-brainer five stars and recommended it to every single person on the face of the earth, YA fan or not. I wish I could tell you I honed my sculpting skills and made a statue of Adornetto, which I proudly displayed as a centerpiece in my living room. Alas, I cannot tell you any one of those things, because not one of them is true. In fact, they’re pretty much the farthest things from true.<br><br>HALO had so many problems: it was waaaaaay too long; the main character was so blatantly dumb, she was deserving of being high-fived in the face with a frying pan, not to mention she was Mary-Sue-perfect; the prose was more purple than my face was while I was reading it; the plot was progressing at the speed of something <i>really</i> slow… That’s only some of its seemingly perpetual list of problems I found. Regardless, I found some moments in the book to be cute and/or funny and/or worthwhile, so I gave it two stars on Goodreads. It’s actually more deserving of one-and-a-half, but who really cares about the semantics?<br><br>The gorgeous and wondrous cover of HALO is reason number one I can prove that theory that first impressions are deceiving.<br><br>The second one is my first impression of HALO carrying over to its much shorter and frankly much better sequel, HADES. HALO was my first impression of Adornetto’s lack of talent, and honestly I would rather gouge my eyes out with a spoon than have to re-read it. HADES is a major step-up from HALO, because while sometimes the plot is shrouded in the shadows of overtly-dumb characters, at least it’s existent. The concept of Hell that Adornetto creates is, to say the least, an epic fail. <span>[image error]</span><br><br>I mean, <i>seriously</i>, Adornetto. Hell is filled to the brim with clubs non-stop partygoers and fancy hotels? Everything I’ve heard about it describes it as a place of eternal torture and suffering, not a place of fun.<br><br>The way she describes the devil is laugh-worthy, and I don’t mean a chuckle, I mean a <span>[image error]</span> kind of laugh. This is what she says to describe him:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>”He wore a white linen suit with a red silk tie and his feet were encased in white cowboy boots. He held an ivory-topped cane that he tapped softly on the cement floor... His skin was tanned and leathery and his eyes were a pellucid blue but devoid of any expression. He was immaculately groomed and wore his silver hair tied back loosely with a gilded clasp."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Yes. I am 100% serious. I am not pranking you. You are not being punk’d (which Bethie made a reference to).<br><br>This brings me to a whole new point . . . Beth.<br><br>Oh, dear <i>Lord</i>, Beth, you are one of the most childish and inexperienced heroines I’ve ever read. You aren’t as bad in this installment as you were in the last one <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <span>[image error]</span>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but you’re still extremely stupid.<br><br>You made so many poor decisions over the course of these books, I’m almost tempted to not read the next book.<br>My first clue you were completely retarded: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I could never do the "'sup nod”—it made me feel as if I were in one of those music videos Molly watched on MTV where men in hoods rapped about “homies” and something called “bling.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And believe me, people. It only gets worse.<br><br>The only reason I say she’s not as bad in this book as she was in HALO is because in this installment, when she’s trapped in Hell, she offers to help two people she’d met there escape when she gets her opportunity to. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Of course, in the end, this is obliviated, but it was still kind of a sweet gesture... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>One thing that completely surprised me about this book is when <b>*kind of SPOILERS, but not really??*</b> Molly declares her love for Gabriel. I SERIOUSLY did not expect that to happen. His reaction is what was really surprising to me. You’re just going to have to read it to get more on that.<br><br>HADES starts off roughly. On one account, the first thirty-five pages has excessive infodump to the point where one of my progress points was solidly<br><br><blockquote>INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP INFODUMP.</blockquote><br><br>I am not exaggerating.<br><br>When Jake introduced the concept of projecting (she could “project” her soul to watch her “loved ones” on Earth while her physical form was still in Hell), I did this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/280711.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously. I did. It was such a BLATANTLY INTRODUCED plot device, I had no other options.<br><br>Not to mention <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Michael <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>'s deus ex machina ending.<br>The cliffhanger at the end had me a bit confused. It was only over the span of one sentence. I have no idea what was going on. Hopefully, HEAVEN (book #3, for those uninformed) will explain what’s goin’ on and what I obviously don’t understand.<br><br>Big improvement from HALO, but there were some . . . <i>obvious</i> . . . problems.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4453132148268309942" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Katie(babs)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs"><img alt="Katie(babs)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242522005p2/179852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154711728?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie(babs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie(babs)" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs">Katie(babs)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/179852-katie-babs?shelf=dnf-award">dnf-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/179852-katie-babs?shelf=gag-worthy-book">gag-worthy-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154711728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6914623340061272803">Hades by Alexandra Adornetto is the sequel to Halo that’s riding the angel train for all its worth. Although I felt Halo was lacking in so many ways, there was some enjoyable moments to it that made me want to pick up Hades. What a big mistake on my end. I feel the only reason Alexandra got published is because of her age. Publishing is giddy when they can find authors under a certain age. They must think they’re sensations, much like pop singers, if the author who’s not of legal age writes a bo</span>
  <span id="freeText6914623340061272803" style="display:none">Hades by Alexandra Adornetto is the sequel to Halo that’s riding the angel train for all its worth. Although I felt Halo was lacking in so many ways, there was some enjoyable moments to it that made me want to pick up Hades. What a big mistake on my end. I feel the only reason Alexandra got published is because of her age. Publishing is giddy when they can find authors under a certain age. They must think they’re sensations, much like pop singers, if the author who’s not of legal age writes a book that can sell like gangbusters. We’ve seen this with Amelia Atwater Rhodes, who was published at fourteen, and recently with Kody Keplinger, where their ages seem to be more important than their writing talent.<br /><br />Hades is such pop light reading and ridiculously tame and simple. I’m not sure whose Alexandra’s audience is. It has an intriguing promise, just like Halo. Uber innocent Bethany Church is one of three angels who must spread her wholesome light and Kumbaya cheer to combat evil and the darkness on Earth. Along the way she falls in love with the human boy, Xavier Woods, but also catches the eye of demon boy, Jake Thorn. When Hades start, Bethany thought she defeated Jacob, but she was wrong. He tricks her into hopping on his motorcycle where he kidnaps her and takes her down to Hell, aka Hades where she’ll be his demon queen. Now Bethany has to figure out a way to get back to Xavier before she succumbs to wearing black lipstick or Daisy Duke shorts as Jake helps her find the dark side she’s hidden deep down inside of her. Too bad Bethany has the personality of a new born kitten. Very cute, but not much else and doesn’t have a mean thought in her head.<br /><br />And that’s were Hades is given the good old DOA label. I’m not sure what Alexandra was trying to accomplish with this book and would love to know what the publisher was thinking when they bought it. There’s nothing worthwhile to recommend here. Alexandra is trying to write something that will appeal to the fans of Meyer’s Twilight, but at least Twilight has some a little bit of originality and soul behind it. The Bethany character reminds me of a clown. A clown must act happy go lucky and always smile when on display. Inside, the clown may be angry or upset but can never show it. That’s Bethany. She has a permanent teeth biting grin on her face while all these mundane yet rascally things happen around her thanks to Jake.<br /><br />Every so often I do like to read about bad boys who show a gentler side when with the heroine. Bad boy suddenly finds a conscience because of the heroine’s love or her magic hoo-haa. (you can blame my romance reading addiction with the rakish hero) But since this is a YA, the heroine’s magic hoo haa doesn’t exist and instead, her magically blinding and optimistic nature is what makes bad boy attracted to her. But alas, Jake is a caricature, a pale vision of what an appealing bad boy should be. Xavier, the good boy, is like one of those cut out cardboard stands you fin at restaurants and in stores.<br /><br />Alexandra’s version of Hell is where one must watch Barney the Dinosaur for all eternity. Hades is painful read with no substance or reason for the story. I can’t see this book selling well at all even with the massive promo Fiewel and Friends are doing for it. I do hope Alexandra has better guidance in the form of a critique partner(or GASP, how about her editor?) because if not, her publishing career may be very short lived.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6914623340061272803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
